<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Donald_Brown_at_2010_UConn_Spring_Game.JPG" class="image"><img alt="refer to caption" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Donald_Brown_at_2010_UConn_Spring_Game.JPG/220px-Donald_Brown_at_2010_UConn_Spring_Game.JPG" width="220" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Donald_Brown_at_2010_UConn_Spring_Game.JPG/330px-Donald_Brown_at_2010_UConn_Spring_Game.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Donald_Brown_at_2010_UConn_Spring_Game.JPG/440px-Donald_Brown_at_2010_UConn_Spring_Game.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1520" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Donald_Brown_at_2010_UConn_Spring_Game.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
2009 International Bowl MVP <a href="/wiki/Donald_Brown_(American_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Donald Brown (American football)">Donald Brown</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For his performance in the 2009 International Bowl, Connecticut running back Donald Brown was named the player of the game. Brown rushed for 261&#160;yards and one&#160;touchdown on 29&#160;attempts.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNrecap_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNrecap-10">[8]</a></sup> He finished the 2008 college football season with 2,083&#160;rushing&#160;yards which led the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTDonaldBrown_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTDonaldBrown-81">[79]</a></sup> Brown set several new UConn school records, including the single-season records for rushing yards (2,083), attempts (367), and yards per game (160.2),<sup id="cite_ref-UConnFBMediaGuideP153_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UConnFBMediaGuideP153-82">[80]</a></sup> the career records for rushing yards (3,800) and attempts (698),<sup id="cite_ref-UConnFBMediaGuideP148_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UConnFBMediaGuideP148-83">[81]</a></sup> and the record for consecutive games with at least 100&#160;yards&#160;rushing (8).<sup id="cite_ref-UConnFBMediaGuideP153_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UConnFBMediaGuideP153-82">[80]</a></sup> His performance did not break the International Bowl rushing record, however; <a href="/wiki/2008_International_Bowl" title="2008 International Bowl">the previous year</a> <a href="/wiki/2007_Rutgers_Scarlet_Knights_football_team" title="2007 Rutgers Scarlet Knights football team">Rutgers</a> running back <a href="/wiki/Ray_Rice" title="Ray Rice">Ray Rice</a> ran for 280&#160;yards and four&#160;touchdowns.<sup id="cite_ref-MSNBC2008IntBowl_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSNBC2008IntBowl-84">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>Brown's dominant rushing performance was supplemented by RB Jordan Todman's 62&#160;yards on seven&#160;attempts, QB Tyler Lorenzen's 32&#160;yards on twelve&#160;attempts, including two&#160;touchdowns, and <a href="/wiki/Fullback_(American_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fullback (American football)">fullback</a> Anthony Sherman's three&#160;yards on one&#160;attempt; in total Connecticut ran for 358&#160;yards. The Huskies attempted to pass only six times during the game; Lorenzen completed four of them for 49&#160;yards and a touchdown. Four different UConn receivers caught one pass each: wide receiver Kashif Moore (18&#160;yards), cornerback and sometime wide receiver Darius Butler (16&#160;yards), fullback Anthony Sherman (11&#160;yards), and tight end Steve Brouse (4&#160;yards and a touchdown).<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNBoxScore_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNBoxScore-85">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Buffalo's offensive performance was in some ways the opposite of Connecticut's: while UConn dominated on the ground and barely passed the ball, Buffalo struggled with the run but had a good day passing. The Bulls ran for a total of 24&#160;yards on the game; James Starks accounted for 25&#160;yards on thirteen&#160;carries and scored a touchdown, while RB Brandon Termilus ran three&#160;times for five&#160;yards. Their total was partially offset by Drew Willy, who lost six&#160;yards on three rushing attempts. Willy had a much more successful day passing, completing 29 out of 43&#160;passes for 213&#160;yards and one&#160;interception. Namaan Roosevelt led the Buffalo receivers with 90&#160;yards on eight&#160;catches; of the five other Bulls who received passes, WR Brett Hamlin caught four&#160;passes for 54&#160;yards, TE Jesse Rack caught three for 22&#160;yards, RB Starks caught 11 for 21&#160;yards, WR Ernest Jackson caught two for 17&#160;yards, and WR Gary Rice caught one for 9&#160;yards.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNBoxScore_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNBoxScore-85">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Connecticut dominated Buffalo statistically in the first half, gaining 225&#160;yards to the Bulls' 94,<sup id="cite_ref-UConnFBMediaGuideP140_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UConnFBMediaGuideP140-8">[6]</a></sup> led by Donald Brown's 208&#160;yards&#160;rushing.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNDonaldBrown1stHalf_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNDonaldBrown1stHalf-86">[84]</a></sup> Buffalo won the turnover battle however, recovering five UConn fumbles. The Bulls scored 20&#160;points off UConn turnovers in the first half, but were held scoreless in the second half when the Huskies stopped turning the ball over.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNBoxScore_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNBoxScore-85">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2009_International_Bowl&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Connecticut's win gave the team a final record of 8–5 and back-to-back winning seasons for the first time since 2003–04.<sup id="cite_ref-CourantUConnTimeline_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CourantUConnTimeline-87">[85]</a></sup> Buffalo's final record fell to 8–6, which still marked the first winning season for the Bulls since transitioning to Division I-A football in 1999.</p>
<p>In a press conference after the game, Brown announced that he would not return for his senior season and enter the NFL Draft, saying he told the media he said he was staying to take the focus off of himself prior to the game.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNrecap_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNrecap-10">[8]</a></sup> Brown was drafted 27th overall by the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a>, becoming the first UConn player ever drafted in the first round. Three other UConn players were drafted in the second round: <a href="/wiki/Darius_Butler" title="Darius Butler">Darius Butler</a> 41st overall by the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Will_Beatty" title="Will Beatty">Will Beatty</a> 60th overall by the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Defensive_end" title="Defensive end">defensive end</a> <a href="/wiki/Cody_Brown" title="Cody Brown">Cody Brown</a> 63rd overall by the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Cardinals" title="Arizona Cardinals">Arizona Cardinals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwichBulletinNFLDraft_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwichBulletinNFLDraft-11">[9]</a></sup> Tight end <a href="/wiki/Martin_B%C3%A9dard" title="Martin Bédard">Martin Bédard</a> was drafted 15th overall in the second round of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">Canadian Football League</a>'s (CFL) <a href="/wiki/2009_CFL_Draft" title="2009 CFL Draft">2009 Draft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2009CFLDraft_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009CFLDraft-88">[86]</a></sup> Buffalo did not have any players drafted by either league in 2009;<sup id="cite_ref-2009CFLDraft_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009CFLDraft-88">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NFLDraft2009Buffalo_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFLDraft2009Buffalo-89">[87]</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/2010_NFL_Draft" title="2010 NFL Draft">2010 NFL Draft</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Starks" title="James Starks">James Starks</a> was selected in the sixth round, 193rd overall, by the <a href="/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay Packers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NFLDraft2010Buffalo_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFLDraft2010Buffalo-90">[88]</a></sup> UConn cornerback <a href="/wiki/Robert_McClain" title="Robert McClain">Robert McClain</a> was also drafted by the NFL in 2010, in the seventh round, 249th overall, by the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NFLDraft2010UConn_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFLDraft2010UConn-91">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MarcusEasleyNote_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarcusEasleyNote-92">[Note 3]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the offseason Connecticut hired <a href="/wiki/Joe_Moorhead" title="Joe Moorhead">Joe Moorhead</a> as their new offensive coordinator, replacing the departed <a href="/wiki/Rob_Ambrose" title="Rob Ambrose">Rob Ambrose</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NorwichBulletinJoeMoorhead_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NorwichBulletinJoeMoorhead-93">[90]</a></sup> Turner Gill returned to coach Buffalo in <a href="/wiki/2009_Buffalo_Bulls_football_team" title="2009 Buffalo Bulls football team">2009</a>. Following that season, however, he left to take over the football program at the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Jayhawks_football" title="Kansas Jayhawks football">University of Kansas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPNTurnerGillKansas_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPNTurnerGillKansas-94">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>Connecticut and Buffalo resumed their rivalry on September 25, <a href="/wiki/2010_NCAA_Division_I_FBS_football_season" title="2010 NCAA Division I FBS football season">2010</a>, playing a regular season game at UConn's <a href="/wiki/Rentschler_Field_(stadium)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rentschler Field (stadium)">Rentschler Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CourantUConn2010Schedule_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CourantUConn2010Schedule-95">[92]</a></sup> Although the score was tied 14–14 at halftime, the Huskies pulled away in the second half after changing quarterbacks, winning the rematch 45–21.<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN2010UConnvsBuffaloRecap_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN2010UConnvsBuffaloRecap-96">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2009_International_Bowl&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Football_League_in_Toronto" title="National Football League in Toronto">National Football League in Toronto</a> – the Bulls were the second football team from Buffalo to play in the Rogers Centre in as many months. On December 7, 2008, the city's <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> team, the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Bills</a>, played a "home" game there against the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimesNFLinToronto_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LATimesNFLinToronto-97">[94]</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/American_football_positions" title="American football positions">American football positions</a></li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2009_International_Bowl&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
